%!TEX root = ../verb-prefixes.tex
%%%
%%% N-conjugation
%%%
\clearpage
\section{\textit{N}-conjugation prefix \textit{n-}}\label{sec:nconj}

\begin{multicols}{2}
\noindent
The \fm{\Af{n}-} conjugation prefix appears in two separate classes of forms:
	(i) progressive aspect forms with \fm{\Af{n}-}
	and (ii) forms with a conjugation prefix \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-} = \fm{\Af{n}-}.
The progressive aspect uses \fm{\Af{n}-} in all verbs regardless of their conjugation class.
This can be seen by (\ref{ex:nconj-prog}) which gives four progressive forms of verbs that belong to each of the four conjugation classes.

\pex\label{ex:nconj-prog}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-prog-0}%
\exrtcmt{∅-conj.\ progressive}%
\begingl
	\gla	Yaa @ \rlap{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}kélʼ.} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	ÿaa= \Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{kelʼ} -μH //
	\glc	along= \Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{undo} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	along \rlap{3>3.\xx{zcnj}.\xx{prog}.undo} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘S/he/it is undoing him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-prog-n}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ progressive}%
\begingl
	\gla	Yaa @ \rlap{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}sʼélʼ.} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	ÿaa= \Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{sʼelʼ} -μH //
	\glc	along= \Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{tear} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	along \rlap{3>3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{prog}.tear} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘S/he/it is tearing him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-prog-gh}%
\exrtcmt{g̱-conj.\ progressive}%
\begingl
	\gla	Yei @ \rlap{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}yísh.} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	yei= \Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{yish} -μH //
	\glc	down= \Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{pull} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	down \rlap{3>3.\xx{g̱cnj}.\xx{prog}.pull} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘S/he/it is pulling down him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-prog-g}%
\exrtcmt{g-conj.\ progressive}%
\begingl
	\gla	Kei @ \rlap{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}tsʼíkʼ.} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	kei= \Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{tsʼikʼ} -μH //
	\glc	up= \Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{pinch} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	up \rlap{3>3.\xx{gcnj}.\xx{prog}.pinch} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘S/he/it is pinching him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\xe

In contrast, forms with \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-} = \fm{\Af{n}-} have the \fm{\Af{n}-} prefix only in verbs that belong to the \fm{n}-conjugation class.
This is shown in (\ref{ex:nconj-imp}) using the same four verbs with imperative mood forms.
Only the \fm{n}-conjugation class verb \fm{aawasʼéil} (\fm{n}; achievement) ‘s/he/it tore him/her/it’ in (\ref{ex:nconj-imp-n}) appears with the \fm{\Af{n}-} prefix.

\pex\label{ex:nconj-imp}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-imp-0}%
\exrtcmt{∅-conj.\ imperative}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Sf{Yi}kélʼ!} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Af{∅} \Sf{yi}- \rt[²]{kelʼ} -μH //
	\glc	\Af{\xx{zcnj}}\· \Sf{\xx{2sg·s}} \rt[²]{undo} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{zcnj}.\xx{imp}.you·guys.undo} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘You guys undo him/her/it!’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-imp-n}%
\ljudge{☞}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ imperative}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Af{N}\Ef{a}\Sf{y}sʼéilʼ!} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Af{n}- \Sf{yi}- \rt[²]{sʼelʼ} -μμH //
	\glc	\Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \Sf{\xx{2sg·s}} \rt[²]{tear} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{imp}.you·guys.tear} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘You guys tear him/her/it!’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-imp-gh}%
\exrtcmt{g̱-conj.\ imperative}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Af{G̱}\Ef{a}\Sf{y}yeesh!} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Af{g̱}- \Sf{yi}- \rt[²]{yish} -μμL //
	\glc	\Af{\xx{g̱cnj}}- \Sf{\xx{2sg·s}} \rt[²]{pull} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{g̱cnj}.\xx{imp}.you·guys.pull} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘You guys pull down him/her/it!’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-imp-g}%
\exrtcmt{g-conj.\ imperative}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Af{G}\Ef{a}\Sf{y}tsʼéekʼ!} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Af{g}- \Sf{yi}- \rt[²]{tsʼikʼ} -μμH //
	\glc	\Af{\xx{gcnj}}- \Sf{\xx{2sg·s}} \rt[²]{pinch} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{gcnj}.\xx{imp}.you·guys.pinch} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘You guys pinch him/her/it!’
		//
\endgl
\xe

There are many contexts where a conjugation prefix \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-} is specified.
All such contexts could specifically have \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-} = \fm{\Af{n}-}.
Some of these contexts also include the irrealis \fm{\Rf{u}-} and/or modal \fm{\Mf{g̱}-} prefixes; these are detailed in subsections \ref{sec:nconj-irrealis} through \ref{sec:nconj-irrealis+modal}.
The seven remaining contexts listed here have \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-} alone without \fm{\Rf{u}-} or \fm{\Mf{g̱}-}:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=0.75em]\raggedyright
\item	imperative mood \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-}
\item	two specialized imperfective aspect types:
	\begin{itemize}
	\item	extensional state imperfective \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-\If{i}-…-μμH/μμL}
	\item	multipositional state imperfective \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-\If{i}-…-k(\:wt\:)}
	\end{itemize}
\item	habitual aspect \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…-ch} (not \fm{∅}-conj.; see sec.\ \ref{sec:pfv})
\item	realizational aspect \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-\If{i}-…-μμH}
\item	consecutive aspect \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…-μμH}
\item	conditional mood \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…-n-í}
\end{itemize}

Of these seven contexts, the extenstional state imperfective, the multipositional state imperfective, and the realizational aspect forms have the \fm{\If{i}-} stative prefix.
The two state imperfectives are lexically specified and the realizational aspect is very rare.
All three are illustrated in (\ref{ex:nconj-i}), with the realizational using the same \fm{n}-conjugation verb as in (\ref{ex:nconj-imp}).

\pex\label{ex:nconj-i}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-i-extstate}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ extensional state impfv.}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Af{N}\Ef{a}\If{a}léi.} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Af{n}- \If{i}- \rt[¹]{leͥ} -μμH //
	\glc	\Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \If{\xx{stv}}- \rt[²]{far} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{impfv}.be.far} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘He/she/it is far, distant.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-i-mposstate}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ multipositional state impfv.}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{Áx̱} @ {} \rlap{\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}dákwt.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	á -x̱ \Af{n}- \If{i}- \rt[¹]{da} -μH -kw -t //
	\glc	\xx{3n} -\xx{pert} \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \Rf{\xx{stv}}- \rt[¹]{flow} -\xx{var} -\xx{rep} -\xx{rep} //
	\gld	it -at \rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{impfv}.be.flow.\xx{mpos}} {} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘They (waters) lie here and there along it.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-i-realizational}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ realizational}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Qf{A}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}sʼéilʼ.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \If{i}- \rt[²]{sʼelʼ} -μμH //
	\glc	\Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \If{\xx{stv}}- \rt[²]{tear} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	\rlap{3>3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{rlzn}.tear} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘S/he/it finally tore him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\xe

The imperative, habitual, consecutive, and conditional lack the \fm{\If{i}-} prefix.
All of these are relatively common and are generally not limited to particular verbs.
The verb of the imperative in (\ref{ex:nconj-prog-n}) is shown with these three other forms in (\ref{ex:nconj-noi}).

\pex\label{ex:nconj-noi}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-noi-habitual}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ habitual}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Qf{A}\Af{n}\Ef{a}sʼélʼch.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{sʼelʼ} -μH -ch //
	\glc	\Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{tear} -\xx{var} -\xx{rep} //
	\gld	\rlap{3>3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{hab}.tear} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘S/he/it always tore him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-noi-consecutive}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ consecutive}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Qf{A}\Af{n}\Ef{a}sʼéilʼ, …} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{sʼelʼ} -μμH {} //
	\glc	\Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{tear} -\xx{var} \xx{sub} //
	\gld	\rlap{3>3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{hab}.tear} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘Her/his/its having finally torn him/her/it, …’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-noi-conditional}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ conditional}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Qf{A}\Af{n}\Ef{a}sʼélʼni, …} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Qf{a}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{sʼelʼ} -μH -n -í //
	\glc	\Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{tear} -\xx{var} -\xx{nsfx} -\xx{sub} //
	\gld	\rlap{3>3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{hab}.tear} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘If s/he/it tears him/her/it, …’
		//
\endgl
\xe

All combinations of the \fm{\Df{d}-} and \fm{\Ff{s}-}/\fm{\Ff{l}-}/\fm{\Ff{sh}-} prefixes are grammatically plausible in this section, but it has yet to be determined if they all actually occur.
\end{multicols}

—			&\Af{n}-	&—		&\Af{n}-		&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Df{d}\If{i}	&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}\If{i}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Df{d}\Ef{a}	&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\
\Qf{a}- arg./expl.	&\Af{n}-	&—		&\Qf{a}-\Af{n}-		&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Df{d}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}		&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\
\Qf{ka}- qualifier	&\Af{n}-	&—		&\Qf{ka}-\Af{n}-	&\?{\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Df{d}\If{i}	&\?{\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}		&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}	&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}	&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\
\Qf{x̱ʼe}- ‘mouth’	&\Af{n}-	&—		&\Qf{x̱ʼe}-\Af{n}-	&\?{\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Df{d}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}	&\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}	&\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}	&\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\
\Qf{ji}- ‘hand’		&\Af{n}-	&—		&\Qf{ji}-\Af{n}-	&\?{\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Df{d}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}		&\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}	&\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}	&\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\
\Qf{tu}- ‘inside’	&\Af{n}-	&—		&\Qf{tu}-\Af{n}-	&\?{\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Df{d}\If{i}}	&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}\If{i}	&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}		&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}	&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}	&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{\textit{N}-conjugation \textit{n-}, unmarked subject (third person or no subject)}
\end{table}

\clearpage
%% N-conjugation, 1SG
\begin{table}
\centerfloat
\begin{tabular}{lccr
		rrrr
		rrrr}
\toprule
			&\multicolumn{2}{c}{Conjunct}	&				&\multicolumn{8}{c}{Classifier prefixes}\\
			\cmidrule(lr){2-3}						\cmidrule(lr){5-12}
Disjunct\rlap{\quad{}+}	& Asp.\rlap{ +}	& Subj.\rlap{ →}& Prefixes			&\Df{d}-\Ff{s}-\If{i}\rlap{-}				&\Df{d}-\If{i}\rlap{-}				&\Ff{s}-\If{i}\rlap{-}				&\Df{d}-				&\Df{d}-\Ff{s}\rlap{-}				&\Ff{s}-				&\If{i}-				&—\\
\midrule
—			&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{x̱}-	&\Af{n}-\Sf{x̱}-			&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Df{d}\If{i}			&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{s}\If{i}			&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Df{d}\Ef{a}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{s}\Ef{a}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ef{a}\If{a}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ef{a}\\
\Qf{a}- expletive	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{x̱}-	&\Qf{a}-\Af{n}-\Sf{x̱}-		&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}		&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Df{d}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Df{d}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{s}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Sf{x̱}\Ef{a}\If{a}		&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Sf{x̱}\Ef{a}\\

\Qf{a}- expletive	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{du}-	&\Qf{a}-\Af{n}-\Sf{du}-		&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\df{\Ff{s}}		&⁎		&\?{\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{a}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\\
\Qf{ka}- qualifier	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{du}-	&\Qf{ka}-\Af{n}-\Sf{du}-	&\?{\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{ka}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\\
\Qf{x̱ʼe}- ‘mouth’	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{du}-	&\Qf{x̱ʼe}-\Af{n}-\Sf{du}-	&\?{\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{x̱ʼa}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\\
\Qf{ji}- ‘hand’		&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{du}-	&\Qf{ji}-\Af{n}-\Sf{du}-	&\?{\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{ji}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\\
\Qf{tu}- ‘inside’	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{du}-	&\Qf{tu}-\Af{n}-\Sf{du}-	&\?{\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{tu}\Af{n}\Sf{du}\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{\textit{N}-conjugation \textit{n-}, fourth person (indefinite) human subject \textit{du-}}
\end{table}

		rccc

\toprule

—			&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-		&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}		&\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Sf{tu}\\
\Qf{ʔa}- expletive	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Qf{ʔa}-\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-	&\?{\Qf{ʔa}\Af{n}\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{ʔa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{ʔa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}		&\Qf{ʔa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\\

\Qf{χʼe}- ‘mouth’	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Qf{χʼe}-\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-	&\?{\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\\
\Qf{tʃi}- ‘hand’	&\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Qf{tʃi}-\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-	&\?{\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\\

\caption{\textit{N}-conjugation /{n-}/, fourth person (indefinite) human subject /{tu-}/, IPA}

%%%
%%% N-conjugation with irrealis
%%%
\clearpage
\subsection{\textit{N}-conjugation prefix \textit{n-} with irrealis \textit{u-}}\label{sec:nconj-irrealis}

\begin{multicols}{2}
\noindent
The \fm{\Af{n}-} conjugation prefix can appear with the irrealis \fm{\Rf{u}-} prefix in several different contexts.
Most such contexts are cases of syntactic irrealis where a syntactic operation has added irrealis to a base form.
All of these syntactic irrealis contexts include a particle preceding the verb, usually at or near the beginning of the sentence.
The prototypical syntactic operation that triggers syntactic irrealis is negation, marked by the addition of the negative particle \fm{tléil} ‘not’.
Other operations of syntactic irrealis include optatives with \fm{gu.aal} ‘hopefully’, prohibitives with \fm{líl} ‘don’t’, and sometimes dubitatives with \fm{gwál} ‘maybe’.
\FIXME{Move discussion of syntactic irrealis to section \ref{sec:zero-irrealis}.}

In addition to the syntactic irrealis contexts, one additional case where \fm{\Rf{u}-} can be found with \fm{\Af{n}-} is the admonitive mood which is formed with \fm{\Rf{u}-\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…-μμH}.
The admonitive is an irrealis-marked counterpart to the realizational formed with \fm{\Af{\xx{cnj}}-\If{i}-…-μμH}, where the irrealis \fm{\Rf{u}-} is added and the stative \fm{\If{i}-} is removed.
Admonitive forms are extremely rare; see Crippen 2019 and Leer 1991 for discussion.
The extract in (\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-admon}) illustrates an admonitive of a \fm{n}-conjugation verb, here \fm{aḵeet} (\fm{∅}/\fm{n}; \fm{-μμL} activity) ‘s/he/it suspects him/her/it’ (this verb can also be a member of the \fm{∅}-conjugation class).

\ex\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-admon}%
\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ admonitive}%
\begingl
	\gla	du \rlap{léelkʼuch} @ {} \rlap{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}ḵéetg̱aa} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	du léelkʼw -ch \Qf{ⱥ}- \Rf{u}- \Af{n}- \rt[²]{ḵit} -μμH {} -g̱áa //
	\glc	\xx{3h·pss} g’parent -\xx{erg} \Qf{\xx{arg}}- \Rf{\xx{irr}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[²]{suspect} -\xx{var} \·\xx{sub} -\xx{ades} //
	\gld	his g’father {} \rlap{3>3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{admon}.suspect} {} {} {} {} {} {} -for //
	\glft	‘lest his grandfather suspect him’
		\trailingcitation{(A.W.\ in Leer 1969: 7.58)}
		//
\endgl
\xe

The following list gives all the contexts where the combination of irrealis \fm{\Rf{u}-} and the \fm{\Af{n}-} conjugation prefix can occur.

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=0.75em]\raggedyright
\item	admonitive mood \fm{\Rf{u}-\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…-μμH}
\item	syntactic irrealis contexts:
	\begin{itemize}
	\item	irrealis progressive aspect \fm{\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-}
	\item	irrealis habitual aspect \fm{\Rf{u}-\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…-ch}
	\item	irrealis specialized state imperfective types:
		\begin{itemize}
		\item	extensional state imperfective \fm{\Rf{u}-\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…μH/μμL}
		\item	multipositional state imperfective \fm{\Rf{u}-\Af{\xx{cnj}}-…-k(wt)}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

The forms in (\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-prog})–(\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-mpos}) illustrate each of the syntactic irrealis contexts using pairs of affirmative and negative.
The progressive aspect uses \fm{\Af{n}-} regardless of conjugation class as discussed earlier in section \ref{sec:nconj}.
This is why \fm{\Af{n}-} appears in (\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-prog}) even though the verb is actually a member of the \fm{∅}-conjugation class, specifically \fm{awlixwétl} (\fm{∅}; achievement) ‘s/he/it made him/her/it tired’.
The other three pairs in (\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-hab})–(\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-mpos}) use \fm{n}-conjugation class verbs.
The habitual in (\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-hab}) is \fm{awlilʼéexʼ} (\fm{n}; achievement) ‘s/he/it broke him/her/it (long)’,
the extensional state imperfective in (\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-ext}) is \fm{naalée} \~\ \fm{naaléi} (\fm{n}; \fm{-μμH} ext.\ state) ‘he/she/it is far, distant’,
and the multipositional state imperfective in (\ref{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-mpos}) is \fm{naadaa} (\fm{n}; \fm{-μμL} ext.\ state) ‘it (fluid) flows’.

\pex\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-prog}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-prog-aff}%
\exrtcmt{affirmative progressive}%
\begingl
	\gla	Yaa \rlap{\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{l}\Ef{a}xwétl.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	ÿaa= \Af{n}- \Sf{x̱}- \Ff{l}- \rt[¹]{xwetl} -μH //
	\glc	along= \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \Sf{\xx{1sg·s}}- \Ff{\xx{csv}}- \rt[¹]{tired} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	along \rlap{3.\xx{zcnj}.\xx{prog}.I.make.tired} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘I am making him/her/it tired.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-prog-neg}%
\exrtcmt{negative progressive}%
\begingl
	\gla	Yaa \rlap{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{l}\Ef{a}xwétl.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	ÿaa= \Rf{u}- \Af{n}- \Sf{x̱}- \Ff{l}- \rt[¹]{xwetl} -μH //
	\glc	along= \Rf{\xx{irr}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \Sf{\xx{1sg·s}}- \Ff{\xx{csv}}- \rt[¹]{tired} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	along \rlap{3.\xx{irr}.\xx{zcnj}.\xx{prog}.I.make.tired} {} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘I am not making him/her/it tired.’
		//
\endgl
\xe

\pex\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-hab}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-hab-aff}%
\exrtcmt{affirmative n-conj.\ habitual}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Af{N}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{l}\Ef{a}lʼíxʼch.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Af{n}- \Sf{x̱}- \Ff{l}- \rt[²]{lʼixʼ} -μH -ch //
	\glc	\Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \Sf{\xx{1sg·s}}- \Ff{\xx{xtn}}- \rt[²]{break} -\xx{var} -\xx{rep} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{hab}.I.make.break} {} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘I have always broken him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-hab-neg}%
\exrtcmt{negative n-conj.\ habitual}%
\begingl
	\gla	Tléil \rlap{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Sf{x̱}\Ff{l}\Ef{a}lʼíxʼch.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	tléil \Rf{u}- \Af{n}- \Sf{x̱}- \Ff{l}- \rt[²]{lʼixʼ} -μH -ch //
	\glc	\Rf{\xx{irr}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \Sf{\xx{1sg·s}}- \Ff{\xx{xtn}}- \rt[²]{break} -\xx{var} -\xx{rep} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{irr}.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{hab}.I.break} {} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘I haven’t broken him/her/it.’
		//
\endgl
\xe

\pex\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-ext}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-ext-aff}%
\exrtcmt{aff.\ n-conj.\ ext.\ state impfv.}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{\Af{N}\Ef{a}\If{a}léi.} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	\Af{n}- \If{i}- \rt[¹]{leͥ} -μμH //
	\glc	\Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \If{\xx{stv}}- \rt[¹]{far} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{impfv}.be.far} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘He/she/it is far, distant.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-ext-neg}%
\exrtcmt{neg.\ n-conj.\ ext.\ state impfv.}%
\begingl
	\gla	Tléil \rlap{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}lé.} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	tléil \Rf{u}- \Af{n}- \rt[¹]{leͥ} -μH //
	\glc	\xx{neg} \Rf{\xx{irr}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[¹]{far} -\xx{var} //
	\gld	not \rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{irr}.\xx{impfv}.be.far} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘He/she/it is not far, distant.’
		//
\endgl
\xe

\pex\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-mpos}%
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-mpos-aff}%
\exrtcmt{aff.\ n-conj.\ mpos.\ state impfv.}%
\begingl
	\gla	\rlap{Áx̱} @ {} \rlap{\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}dákwt.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	á -x̱ \Af{n}- \If{i}- \rt[¹]{da} -μH -kw -t //
	\glc	\xx{3n} -\xx{pert} \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \Rf{\xx{stv}}- \rt[¹]{flow} -\xx{var} -\xx{rep} -\xx{rep} //
	\gld	it -at \rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{impfv}.be.flow.\xx{mpos}} {} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘They (waters) lie here and there along it.’
		//
\endgl
\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-mpos-neg}%
\exrtcmt{neg.\ n-conj.\ mpos.\ state impfv.}%
\begingl
	\gla	Tléil \rlap{áx̱} @ {} \rlap{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}dákwt.} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} @ {} //
	\glb	tléil á -x̱ \Rf{u}- \Af{n}- \rt[¹]{da} -μH -kw -t //
	\glc	\xx{neg} \xx{3n} -\xx{pert} \Rf{\xx{irr}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \rt[¹]{flow} -\xx{var} -\xx{rep} -\xx{rep} //
	\gld	not it -at \rlap{3.\xx{irr}.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{impfv}.be.flow.\xx{mpos}} {} {} {} {} {} //
	\glft	‘They (waters) do not lie here and there along it.’
		//
\endgl
\xe

\FIXME{Discuss problem of \fm{\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-} with \fm{\If{i}-}.
Does this actually occur?
Maybe not because all syntactic \fm{\Rf{u}-} also involves suppressing \fm{\If{i}-}.
That doesn’t exclude the still outstanding \fm{\Rf{w}-} (cf.\ prospective aspect).
This mostly occurs in unmarked aspect but there are at least a few cases that look like \fm{\Rf{w}-\Af{n}-\If{i}-}.
Maybe all comparatives with \fm{\Qf{ka}-} \~\ \fm{\Qf{ga}-} as \fm{\Qf{k}\Rf{u}} not \fm[*]{\Qf{ko}\Rf{o}}.
Also in extraordinary states (Crippen 2019: 655) e.g.\ \fm{\Qf{k}\Rf{u}\Ff{l}\If{i}téesʼshán} ‘it is fascinating to watch’.
May only occur with \fm{\Qf{ka}-}, \fm{\Qf{ÿa}-}, and \fm{\Qf{ka}-} \~\ \fm{\Qf{ga}-} comparative.
Didn’t see any forms with \fm{\Qf{x̱ʼe}-}, \fm{\Qf{shu}-}, \fm{\Qf{tu}-}, \fm{\Qf{ḵu}-}, \fm{\Qf{ji}-}.}

\FIXME{Other cases of \fm{\Rf{w}-} include indirect motion derivations (Crippen 2019: 609–612, 653) e.g.\ \fm{\Qf{a}\Qf{w}\Rf{u}\Df{d}\Ef{a}gútx̱} not \fm[*]{\Qf{a}\Qf{wo}\Rf{o}\Df{d}\Ef{a}gútx̱} with \fm{\Qf{ÿa}-}, but these lack \fm{\If{i}-}.
Maybe also with self-benefactive \fm{\Qf{g}-} in \fm{tléil \Qf{g}\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{l}}chéesh}.
Investigate forms with \fm{\Qf{k}\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}} — \fm{akunalx̱úx̱ch}, \fm{akunal.éexʼch}, \fm{akunanáach}.
These look like habituals but the \fm{u} is unexpected.}

%  Chʼa yeisú l unaliyéit has u.aatjí (011 Tom Peters: 53)
%
%\pex\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-cmpvext}%
%\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-cmpvext-normal}%
%\exrtcmt{n-conj.\ ext.\ state impfv.}%
%\begingl

%	\glc	\Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \If{\xx{stv}}- \rt[¹]{far} -\xx{var} //
%	\gld	\rlap{3.\xx{ncnj}.\xx{impfv}.be.far} {} {} {} //
%	\glft	‘He/she/it is far, distant.’
%		//
%\endgl
%\a\label{ex:nconj-irrealis-synx-cmpvext-normal}%
%\exrtcmt{cmpv.\ n-conj.\ ext.\ state impfv.}%
%\begingl

%	\glc	\xx{3n} \xx{sim} \Qf{\xx{cmpv}}- \Rf{\xx{irr}}- \Af{\xx{ncnj}}- \If{\xx{stv}}- \rt[¹]{far} -\xx{var} //

%\endgl

\end{multicols}

\clearpage
%% N-conjugation, Irrealis, 3
\begin{table}
\centerfloat
\begin{tabular}{lccr
		rrrr
		rrrr}
\toprule
			&\multicolumn{2}{c}{Conjunct}	&				&\multicolumn{8}{c}{Classifier prefixes}\\
			\cmidrule(lr){2-3}						\cmidrule(lr){5-12}
Disjunct\rlap{\quad{}+}	& Asp.\rlap{ +}	& Subj.\rlap{ →}& Prefixes			&\Df{d}-\Ff{s}-\If{i}\rlap{-}			&\Df{d}-\If{i}\rlap{-}			&\Ff{s}-\If{i}\rlap{-}			&\Df{d}-				&\Df{d}-\Ff{s}\rlap{-}			&\Ff{s}-				&\If{i}-				&—\\
\midrule
—			&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-	&—		&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-			&\?{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}		&\?{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Df{d}\If{i}}		&\?{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ff{s}\If{i}}		&\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ef{a}		&\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}		&\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}		&\?{\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}}		&\Rf{u}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\
\Qf{a}- arg./expl.	&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-	&—		&\Qf{a}-\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-		&\?{\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ff{z}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Df{d}\If{i}}	&\?{\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Df{d}\Ef{a}		&\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}	&\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Ff{s}		&\?{\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\If{a}}	&\Qf{o}\Rf{o}\Af{n}\Ef{a}\\

\Qf{kʰa}- qualifier	&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Qf{kʰa}-\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-	&\?{\Qf{kʰa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{kʰa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{kʰa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{kʰa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\\
\Qf{χʼe}- ‘mouth’	&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Qf{χʼe}-\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-	&\?{\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{χʼa}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\\
\Qf{tʃi}- ‘hand’	&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Qf{tʃi}-\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-	&\?{\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{tʃi}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\\
\Qf{tʰu}- ‘inside’	&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-	&\Sf{tu}-	&\Qf{tʰu}-\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-\Sf{tu}-	&\?{\Qf{tʰu}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&⁎			&⁎			&⁎		&\Qf{tʰu}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\df{\Ff{s}}	&⁎		&\?{\Qf{tʰu}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}.\If{w}\Ef{a}}	&\Qf{tʰu}\Af{n}.\Sf{tu}\\

—			&\Af{n}-\Mf{q}-	&\Sf{χ}-	&\Af{n}-\Mf{q}-\Sf{χ}-		&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}}			&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}.\Df{t}\If{i}}	&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}.\Ff{s}\If{i}}	&\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}.\Df{t}\Ef{a}	&\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}\df{\Ff{s}}	&\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}.\Ff{s}\Ef{a}	&\?{\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}\If{ː}}	&\Af{n}\Ef{a}.\Mf{q}\Sf{ʰ}\Ef{a}\\

\Qf{χʼe}- ‘mouth’	&\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-\Mf{q}-	&\Sf{ji}-	&\Qf{χʼe}-\Rf{u}-\Af{n}-\Mf{q}-\Sf{ji}-	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{ji}.\Df{t}\Ff{s}\If{i}	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{ji}.\Df{t}\If{i}	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{ji}.\Ff{s}\If{i}	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{ji}.\Df{t}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{ji}\df{\Ff{s}}	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{ji}.\Ff{s}\Ef{a}	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{jiː}\If{j}	&\Qf{χʼa}.\Af{n}\Ef{a}\Mf{χ}.\Sf{ji}\\
